The match was nicknamed "Thunder Meets Lightning" as an allusion to punching power of Ch\xc3\xa1vez and blinding speed of Taylor. Ch\xc3\xa1vez was the epitome of the "Mexican" style of boxing. Taylor\'s hand and foot speed and boxing abilities gave him the early advantage, allowing him to begin building a large lead on points. Ch\xc3\xa1vez remained relentless in his pursuit of Taylor and due to his greater punching power Ch\xc3\xa1vez slowly punished Taylor. Coming into the later rounds, Taylor was bleeding from the mouth, his entire face was swollen, the bones around his eye socket had been broken, he had swallowed a considerable amount of his own blood, and as he grew tired, Taylor was increasingly forced into exchanging blows with Ch\xc3\xa1vez, which only gave Ch\xc3\xa1vez a greater chance to cause damage. While there was little doubt that Taylor had solidly won the first three quarters of the fight, the question at hand was whether he would survive the final quarter. Going into the final round, Taylor held a secure lead on the scorecards of two of the three judges. Ch\xc3\xa1vez would have to knock Taylor out to claim a victory, whereas Taylor merely needed to stay away from the Mexican legend. However, Taylor did not stay away, but continued to trade blows with Ch\xc3\xa1vez. As he did so, Taylor showed signs of extreme exhaustion, and every tick of the clock brought Taylor closer to victory unless Ch\xc3\xa1vez could knock him out.\nWith about a minute left in the round, Ch\xc3\xa1vez hit Taylor squarely with several hard punches and stayed on the attack, continuing to hit Taylor with well-placed shots. Finally, with about 25 seconds to go, Ch\xc3\xa1vez landed a hard right hand that caused Taylor to stagger forward towards a corner, forcing Ch\xc3\xa1vez back ahead of him. Suddenly Ch\xc3\xa1vez stepped around Taylor, positioning him so that Taylor was trapped in the corner, with no way to escape from Ch\xc3\xa1vez\' desperate final flurry. Ch\xc3\xa1vez then nailed Taylor with a tremendous right hand that dropped the younger man. By using the ring ropes to pull himself up, Taylor managed to return to his feet and was given the mandatory 8-count. Referee Richard Steele asked Taylor twice if he was able to continue fighting, but Taylor failed to answer. Steele then concluded that Taylor was unfit to continue and signaled that he was ending the fight, resulting in a TKO victory for Ch\xc3\xa1vez with only two seconds to go in the bout.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Since boxing involves forceful, repetitive punching, precautions must be taken to prevent <a href="/wiki/Boxer%27s_fracture" title="Boxer&#39;s fracture">damage to bones in the hand</a>. Most trainers do not allow boxers to train and spar without <a href="/wiki/Wrist_wraps" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrist wraps">wrist wraps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boxing_gloves" class="mw-redirect" title="Boxing gloves">boxing gloves</a>. Hand wraps are used to secure the bones in the hand, and the gloves are used to protect the hands from blunt injury, allowing boxers to throw punches with more force than if they did not use them. Gloves have been required in competition since the late nineteenth century, though modern boxing gloves are much heavier than those worn by early twentieth-century fighters. Prior to a bout, both boxers agree upon the weight of gloves to be used in the bout, with the understanding that lighter gloves allow heavy punchers to inflict more damage. The brand of gloves can also affect the impact of punches, so this too is usually stipulated before a bout. Both sides are allowed to inspect the wraps and gloves of the opponent to help ensure both are within agreed upon specifications and no tampering has taken place.\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Mouthguard" title="Mouthguard">mouthguard</a> is important to protect the teeth and gums from injury, and to cushion the jaw, resulting in a decreased chance of knockout. Both fighters must wear soft soled shoes to reduce the damage from accidental (or intentional) stepping on feet. While older boxing boots more commonly resembled those of a professional wrestler, modern boxing shoes and boots tend to be quite similar to their amateur wrestling counterparts.\n</p><p>Boxers practice their skills on several types of punching bags. A small, tear-drop-shaped "speed bag" is used to hone reflexes and repetitive punching skills, while a large cylindrical "heavy bag" filled with sand, a synthetic substitute, or water is used to practice power punching and body blows. The double-end bag is usually connected by elastic on the top and bottom and moves randomly upon getting struck and helps the fighter work on accuracy and reflexes. In addition to these distinctive pieces of equipment, boxers also use sport-nonspecific training equipment to build strength, speed, agility, and stamina. Common training equipment includes free weights, rowing machines, <a href="/wiki/Jump_rope" class="mw-redirect" title="Jump rope">jump rope</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Medicine_balls" class="mw-redirect" title="Medicine balls">medicine balls</a>. \n</p><p>Boxers also use punch/focus mitts in which a trainer calls out certain combinations and the fighter strikes the mitts accordingly. This is a great exercise for stamina as the boxer isn\'t allowed to go at his own pace but that of the trainer, typically forcing the fighter to endure a higher output and volume than usual. In addition, they also allow trainers to make boxers utilize footwork and distances more accurately.\n</p><p>Boxing matches typically take place in a <a href="/wiki/Boxing_ring" title="Boxing ring">boxing ring</a>, a raised platform surrounded by ropes attached to posts rising in each corner. The term "ring" has come to be used as a metaphor for many aspects of prize fighting in general.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technique">Technique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Technique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Boxing_styles_and_technique" title="Boxing styles and technique">Boxing styles and technique</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stance">Stance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Stance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The modern boxing stance differs substantially from the typical boxing stances of the 19th and early 20th centuries. The modern stance has a more upright vertical-armed guard, as opposed to the more horizontal, knuckles-facing-forward guard adopted by early 20th century hook users such as <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(boxer)" title="Jack Johnson (boxer)">Jack Johnson</a>.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Attitude_droite1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Attitude_droite1.jpg/103px-Attitude_droite1.jpg" width="103" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Attitude_droite1.jpg/154px-Attitude_droite1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Attitude_droite1.jpg/206px-Attitude_droite1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="1196" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i>Upright stance</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/70px-Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg" width="70" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/106px-Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/141px-Attitude_semi-enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="611" data-file-height="1040" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i>Semi-crouch</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/60px-Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg" width="60" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/90px-Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg/120px-Attitude_enroul%C3%A9e1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="534" data-file-height="1062" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i>Full crouch</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<p>In a fully upright stance, the boxer stands with the legs shoulder-width apart and the rear foot a half-step in front of the lead man. Right-handed or orthodox boxers lead with the left foot and fist (for most penetration power). Both feet are parallel, and the right heel is off the ground. The lead (left) fist is held vertically about six inches in front of the face at eye level. The rear (right) fist is held beside the chin and the elbow tucked against the ribcage to protect the body. The chin is tucked into the chest to avoid punches to the jaw which commonly cause knock-outs and is often kept slightly off-center. Wrists are slightly bent to avoid damage when punching and the elbows are kept tucked in to protect the ribcage. Some boxers fight from a crouch, leaning forward and keeping their feet closer together. The stance described is considered the "textbook" stance and fighters are encouraged to change it around once it\'s been mastered as a base. Case in point, many fast fighters have their hands down and have almost exaggerated footwork, while brawlers or bully fighters tend to slowly stalk their opponents.\n</p><p>Left-handed or southpaw fighters use a mirror image of the orthodox stance, which can create problems for orthodox fighters unaccustomed to receiving jabs, hooks, or crosses from the opposite side. The <a href="/wiki/Southpaw_stance" title="Southpaw stance">southpaw stance</a>, conversely, is vulnerable to a straight right hand.\n</p><p>North American fighters tend to favor a more balanced stance, facing the opponent almost squarely, while many European fighters stand with their torso turned more to the side. The positioning of the hands may also vary, as some fighters prefer to have both hands raised in front of the face, risking exposure to body shots.\n</p><p>Modern boxers can sometimes be seen tapping their cheeks or foreheads with their fists in order to remind themselves to keep their hands up (which becomes difficult during long bouts). Boxers are taught to push off with their feet in order to move effectively. Forward motion involves lifting the lead leg and pushing with the rear leg. Rearward motion involves lifting the rear leg and pushing with the lead leg. During lateral motion the leg in the direction of the movement moves first while the opposite leg provides the force needed to move the body.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punches">Punches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Punches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are four basic punches in boxing: the jab, cross, hook and uppercut. Any punch other than a jab is considered a power punch. If a boxer is right-handed (orthodox), his left hand is the lead hand and his right hand is the rear hand. For a left-handed boxer or southpaw, the hand positions are reversed. For clarity, the following discussion will assume a right-handed boxer.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:26px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jab7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jab7.jpg/105px-Jab7.jpg" width="105" height="98" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jab7.jpg/158px-Jab7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Jab7.jpg/210px-Jab7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1127" data-file-height="1053" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Jab" title="Jab">Jab</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:23.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Drop3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Drop3.jpg/105px-Drop3.jpg" width="105" height="103" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Drop3.jpg/158px-Drop3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Drop3.jpg/210px-Drop3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1001" data-file-height="983" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Cross_(boxing)" title="Cross (boxing)">Cross</a> </i> - in counter-punch with a looping\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Crochet1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Crochet1.jpg/104px-Crochet1.jpg" width="104" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Crochet1.jpg/156px-Crochet1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Crochet1.jpg/209px-Crochet1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="972" data-file-height="1118" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Hook_(boxing)" title="Hook (boxing)">Hook</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:22.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uppercut2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Uppercut2.jpg/105px-Uppercut2.jpg" width="105" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Uppercut2.jpg/158px-Uppercut2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Uppercut2.jpg/210px-Uppercut2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="1047" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Uppercut" title="Uppercut">Uppercut</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Jab" title="Jab">Jab</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 A quick, straight punch thrown with the lead hand from the guard position. The jab is accompanied by a small, clockwise rotation of the torso and hips, while the fist rotates 90 degrees, becoming horizontal upon impact. As the punch reaches full extension, the lead shoulder can be brought up to guard the chin. The rear hand remains next to the face to guard the jaw. After making contact with the target, the lead hand is retracted quickly to resume a guard position in front of the face.\n<ul><li>The jab is recognized as the most important punch in a boxer\'s arsenal because it provides a fair amount of its own cover and it leaves the least amount of space for a counter punch from the opponent. It has the longest reach of any punch and does not require commitment or large weight transfers. Due to its relatively weak power, the jab is often used as a tool to gauge distances, probe an opponent\'s defenses, harass an opponent, and set up heavier, more powerful punches. A half-step may be added, moving the entire body into the punch, for additional power. Some notable boxers who have been able to develop relative power in their jabs and use it to punish or \'wear down\' their opponents to some effect include <a href="/wiki/Larry_Holmes" title="Larry Holmes">Larry Holmes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_Klitschko" title="Wladimir Klitschko">Wladimir Klitschko</a>.</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Cross_(boxing)" title="Cross (boxing)">Cross</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 A powerful, straight punch thrown with the rear hand. From the guard position, the rear hand is thrown from the chin, crossing the body and traveling towards the target in a straight line. The rear shoulder is thrust forward and finishes just touching the outside of the chin. At the same time, the lead hand is retracted and tucked against the face to protect the inside of the chin. For additional power, the torso and hips are rotated counter-clockwise as the cross is thrown. A measure of an ideally extended cross is that the shoulder of the striking arm, the knee of the front leg and the ball of the front foot are on the same vertical plane.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n<ul><li>Weight is also transferred from the rear foot to the lead foot, resulting in the rear heel turning outwards as it acts as a fulcrum for the transfer of weight. Body rotation and the sudden weight transfer is what gives the cross its power. Like the jab, a half-step forward may be added. After the cross is thrown, the hand is retracted quickly and the guard position resumed. It can be used to counter punch a jab, aiming for the opponent\'s head (or a counter to a cross aimed at the body) or to set up a hook. The cross is also called a "straight" or "right", especially if it does not cross the opponent\'s outstretched jab.</li></ul></li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Hook_(boxing)" title="Hook (boxing)">Hook</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 A semi-circular punch thrown with the lead hand to the side of the opponent\'s head. From the guard position, the elbow is drawn back with a horizontal fist (palm facing down) though in modern times a wide percentage of fighters throw the hook with a vertical fist (palm facing themselves). The rear hand is tucked firmly against the jaw to protect the chin. The torso and hips are rotated clockwise, propelling the fist through a tight, clockwise arc across the front of the body and connecting with the target.\n<ul><li>At the same time, the lead foot pivots clockwise, turning the left heel outwards. Upon contact, the hook\'s circular path ends abruptly and the lead hand is pulled quickly back into the guard position. A hook may also target the lower body and this technique is sometimes called the "rip" to distinguish it from the conventional hook to the head. The hook may also be thrown with the rear hand. Notable left hookers include <a href="/wiki/Joe_Frazier" title="Joe Frazier">Joe Frazier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Jones,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Roy Jones, Jr.">Roy Jones Jr.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg/220px-Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg/330px-Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg/440px-Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1797" data-file-height="1110" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boxing080905_photoshop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Dominguez" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricardo Dominguez">Ricardo Dominguez</a> (<i>left</i>) throws an <a href="/wiki/Uppercut" title="Uppercut">uppercut</a> on <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rafael_Ortiz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rafael Ortiz (page does not exist)">Rafael Ortiz</a> (<i>right</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Uppercut" title="Uppercut">Uppercut</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 A vertical, rising punch thrown with the rear hand. From the guard position, the torso shifts slightly to the right, the rear hand drops below the level of the opponent\'s chest and the knees are bent slightly. From this position, the rear hand is thrust upwards in a rising arc towards the opponent\'s chin or torso.\n<ul><li>At the same time, the knees push upwards quickly and the torso and hips rotate anti-clockwise and the rear heel turns outward, mimicking the body movement of the cross. The strategic utility of the uppercut depends on its ability to "lift" the opponent\'s body, setting it off-balance for successive attacks. The right uppercut followed by a left hook is a deadly combination employing the uppercut to lift the opponent\'s chin into a vulnerable position, then the hook to knock the opponent out.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<p>These different punch types can be thrown in rapid succession to form combinations or "combos." The most common is the jab and cross combination, nicknamed the "one-two combo." This is usually an effective combination, because the jab blocks the opponent\'s view of the cross, making it easier to land cleanly and forcefully.\n</p><p>A large, swinging circular punch starting from a cocked-back position with the arm at a longer extension than the hook and all of the fighter\'s weight behind it is sometimes referred to as a "roundhouse," "haymaker," "overhand," or sucker-punch. Relying on body weight and centripetal force within a wide arc, the roundhouse can be a powerful blow, but it is often a wild and uncontrolled punch that leaves the fighter delivering it off balance and with an open guard.\n</p><p>Wide, looping punches have the further disadvantage of taking more time to deliver, giving the opponent ample warning to react and counter. For this reason, the haymaker or roundhouse is not a conventional punch, and is regarded by trainers as a mark of poor technique or desperation. Sometimes it has been used, because of its immense potential power, to finish off an already staggering opponent who seems unable or unlikely to take advantage of the poor position it leaves the puncher in.\n</p><p>Another unconventional punch is the rarely used <a href="/wiki/Bolo_punch" title="Bolo punch">bolo punch</a>, in which the opponent swings an arm out several times in a wide arc, usually as a distraction, before delivering with either that or the other arm.\n</p><p>An illegal punch to the back of the head or neck is known as a <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_punch" title="Rabbit punch">rabbit punch</a>.\n</p><p>Both the hook and uppercut may be thrown with both hands, resulting in differing footwork and positioning from that described above if thrown by the other hand. Generally the analogous opposite is true of the footwork and torso movement.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Defense">Defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>There are several basic maneuvers a boxer can use in order to evade or block punches, depicted and discussed below.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:23px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slip1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Slip1.jpg/105px-Slip1.jpg" width="105" height="104" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Slip1.jpg/158px-Slip1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Slip1.jpg/210px-Slip1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="589" data-file-height="586" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Slipping" title="Slipping">Slipping</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:15.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Slip2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Slip2.jpg/105px-Slip2.jpg" width="105" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Slip2.jpg/158px-Slip2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Slip2.jpg/210px-Slip2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1052" data-file-height="1196" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Bobbing_(boxing)" title="Bobbing (boxing)">Bobbing</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:29px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blocage1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Blocage1.jpg/105px-Blocage1.jpg" width="105" height="92" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Blocage1.jpg/158px-Blocage1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Blocage1.jpg/210px-Blocage1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1199" data-file-height="1047" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Blocking_(martial_arts)" title="Blocking (martial arts)">Blocking</a> (with the arms)</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:25px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Protection_passive1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protection_passive1.jpg/105px-Protection_passive1.jpg" width="105" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protection_passive1.jpg/158px-Protection_passive1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Protection_passive1.jpg/210px-Protection_passive1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="843" data-file-height="801" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Covering_(martial_arts)" title="Covering (martial arts)">Cover-Up</a> (with the gloves)</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Neutraliser1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Neutraliser1.jpg/103px-Neutraliser1.jpg" width="103" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Neutraliser1.jpg/154px-Neutraliser1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Neutraliser1.jpg/206px-Neutraliser1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="899" data-file-height="1047" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Clinch_fighting" title="Clinch fighting">Clinching</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:28px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pas_de_retrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Pas_de_retrait.jpg/105px-Pas_de_retrait.jpg" width="105" height="94" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Pas_de_retrait.jpg/158px-Pas_de_retrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Pas_de_retrait.jpg/210px-Pas_de_retrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="955" data-file-height="857" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Footwork_(martial_arts)" title="Footwork (martial arts)">Footwork</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 140px"><div style="width: 140px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 135px;"><div style="margin:20px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Retrait2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Retrait2.jpg/105px-Retrait2.jpg" width="105" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Retrait2.jpg/158px-Retrait2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Retrait2.jpg/210px-Retrait2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="978" data-file-height="1029" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i>Pulling away</i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<ul><li><b>Slip</b> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Slipping" title="Slipping">Slipping</a> rotates the body slightly so that an incoming punch passes harmlessly next to the head. As the opponent\'s punch arrives, the boxer sharply rotates the hips and shoulders. This turns the chin sideways and allows the punch to "slip" past. <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a> was famous for extremely fast and close slips, as was an early <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>.</li>\n<li><b>Sway or fade</b> \xe2\x80\x93 To anticipate a punch and move the upper body or head back so that it misses or has its force appreciably lessened. Also called "rolling with the punch" or " Riding The Punch".</li>\n<li><b>Duck</b> or <b>break</b> \xe2\x80\x93 To drop down with the back straight so that a punch aimed at the head glances or misses entirely.</li>\n<li><b>Bob and weave</b> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Bobbing_(boxing)" title="Bobbing (boxing)">Bobbing</a> moves the head laterally and beneath an incoming punch. As the opponent\'s punch arrives, the boxer bends the legs quickly and simultaneously shifts the body either slightly right or left. Once the punch has been evaded, the boxer "weaves" back to an upright position, emerging on either the outside or inside of the opponent\'s still-extended arm. To move outside the opponent\'s extended arm is called "bobbing to the outside". To move inside the opponent\'s extended arm is called "bobbing to the inside". Joe Frazier, Jack Dempsey, Mike Tyson and Rocky Marciano were masters of bobbing and weaving.</li>\n<li><b>Parry/block</b> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Parrying" class="mw-redirect" title="Parrying">Parrying</a> or <a href="/wiki/Blocking_(martial_arts)" title="Blocking (martial arts)">blocking</a> uses the boxer\'s shoulder, hands or arms as defensive tools to protect against incoming attacks. A block generally receives a punch while a parry tends to deflect it. A "palm", "catch", or "cuff" is a defence which intentionally takes the incoming punch on the palm portion of the defender\'s glove.</li>\n<li><b>The cover-up</b> \xe2\x80\x93 Covering up is the last opportunity (other than rolling with a punch) to avoid an incoming strike to an unprotected face or body. Generally speaking, the hands are held high to protect the head and chin and the forearms are tucked against the torso to impede body shots. When protecting the body, the boxer rotates the hips and lets incoming punches "roll" off the guard. To protect the head, the boxer presses both fists against the front of the face with the forearms parallel and facing outwards. This type of guard is weak against attacks from below.</li>\n<li>The <b><a href="/wiki/Grappling_position#Stand-up_positions" title="Grappling position">clinch</a></b> \xe2\x80\x93 Clinching is a form of <a href="/wiki/Trapping_(martial_arts)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trapping (martial arts)">trapping</a> or a rough form of <a href="/wiki/Grappling" title="Grappling">grappling</a> and occurs when the distance between both fighters has closed and straight punches cannot be employed. In this situation, the boxer attempts to <a href="/wiki/Grappling_hold" title="Grappling hold">hold</a> or "tie up" the opponent\'s hands so he is unable to throw hooks or <a href="/wiki/Uppercut" title="Uppercut">uppercuts</a>. To perform a clinch, the boxer loops both hands around the outside of the opponent\'s shoulders, scooping back under the forearms to grasp the opponent\'s arms tightly against his own body. In this position, the opponent\'s arms are pinned and cannot be used to attack. <a href="/wiki/Clinching_position" class="mw-redirect" title="Clinching position">Clinching</a> is a temporary match state and is quickly dissipated by the referee. Clinching is technically against the rules, and in amateur fights points are deducted fairly quickly for it. It is unlikely, however, to see points deducted for a clinch in professional boxing.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Less_common_strategies">Less common strategies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Less common strategies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li><b>The "<a href="/wiki/Rope-a-dope" title="Rope-a-dope">rope-a-dope</a>" strategy</b>&#160;: Used by Muhammad Ali in his 1974 "<a href="/wiki/The_Rumble_in_the_Jungle" title="The Rumble in the Jungle">the Rumble in the Jungle</a>" bout against George Foreman, the rope-a-dope method involves lying back against the ropes, covering up defensively as much as possible and allowing the opponent to attempt numerous punches. The back-leaning posture, which does not cause the defending boxer to become as unbalanced as he would during normal backward movement, also maximizes the distance of the defender\'s head from his opponent, increasing the probability that punches will miss their intended target. Weathering the blows that do land, the defender lures the opponent into expending energy while conserving his/her own. If successful, the attacking opponent will eventually tire, creating defensive flaws which the boxer can exploit. In modern boxing, the rope-a-dope is generally discouraged since most opponents are not fooled by it and few boxers possess the physical toughness to withstand a prolonged, unanswered assault. Recently, however, <a href="/wiki/Octuple_champion" title="Octuple champion">eight-division world champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Manny_Pacquiao" title="Manny Pacquiao">Manny Pacquiao</a> skillfully used the strategy to gauge the power of welterweight titlist <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cotto" title="Miguel Cotto">Miguel Cotto</a> in November 2009. Pacquiao followed up the rope-a-dope gambit with a withering knockdown.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Bolo_punch" title="Bolo punch">Bolo punch</a></b>&#160;: Occasionally seen in Olympic boxing, the bolo is an arm punch which owes its power to the shortening of a <a href="/wiki/Circular_arc" class="mw-redirect" title="Circular arc">circular arc</a> rather than to transference of body weight; it tends to have more of an effect due to the surprise of the odd angle it lands at rather than the actual power of the punch. This is more of a gimmick than a technical maneuver; this punch is not taught, being on the same plane in boxing technicality as is the <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Ali shuffle</a>. Nevertheless, a few professional boxers have used the bolo-punch to great effect, including former <a href="/wiki/Welterweight" title="Welterweight">welterweight</a> champions <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray_Leonard" title="Sugar Ray Leonard">Sugar Ray Leonard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kid_Gavilan" class="mw-redirect" title="Kid Gavilan">Kid Gavilan</a>. Middleweight champion <a href="/wiki/Ceferino_Garcia" title="Ceferino Garcia">Ceferino Garcia</a> is regarded as the inventor of the bolo punch.</li></ul>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Contre_bolo1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Contre_bolo1.jpg/114px-Contre_bolo1.jpg" width="114" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Contre_bolo1.jpg/171px-Contre_bolo1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Contre_bolo1.jpg/229px-Contre_bolo1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="979" data-file-height="1028" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Bolo_punch" title="Bolo punch">Bolo punch</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Drop1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Drop1.jpg/100px-Drop1.jpg" width="100" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Drop1.jpg/150px-Drop1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Drop1.jpg/200px-Drop1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="942" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><i><a href="/wiki/Overhand_(boxing)" title="Overhand (boxing)">Overhand (overcut)</a></i>\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Drop_(boxing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Drop (boxing)">Overhand right</a></b>&#160;: The overhand right is a punch not found in every boxer\'s arsenal. Unlike the right cross, which has a trajectory parallel to the ground, the overhand right has a looping circular arc as it is thrown over the shoulder with the palm facing away from the boxer. It is especially popular with smaller stature boxers trying to reach taller opponents. Boxers who have used this punch consistently and effectively include former heavyweight champions <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Marciano" title="Rocky Marciano">Rocky Marciano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Witherspoon" title="Tim Witherspoon">Tim Witherspoon</a>, as well as MMA champions <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Liddell" title="Chuck Liddell">Chuck Liddell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fedor_Emelianenko" title="Fedor Emelianenko">Fedor Emelianenko</a>. The overhand right has become a popular weapon in other tournaments that involve fist striking.</li>\n<li><b><a href="/wiki/Check_hook" title="Check hook">Check hook</a></b>&#160;: A check hook is employed to prevent aggressive boxers from lunging in. There are two parts to the check hook. The first part consists of a regular hook. The second, trickier part involves the footwork. As the opponent lunges in, the boxer should throw the hook and pivot on his left foot and swing his right foot 180 degrees around. If executed correctly, the aggressive boxer will lunge in and sail harmlessly past his opponent like a bull missing a matador. This is rarely seen in professional boxing as it requires a great disparity in skill level to execute. Technically speaking it has been said that there is no such thing as a check hook and that it is simply a hook applied to an opponent that has lurched forward and past his opponent who simply hooks him on the way past. Others have argued that the check hook exists but is an illegal punch due to it being a pivot punch which is illegal in the sport. <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Mayweather,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Floyd Mayweather, Jr.">Floyd Mayweather, Jr.</a> employed the use of a check hook against <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Hatton" title="Ricky Hatton">Ricky Hatton</a>, which sent Hatton flying head first into the corner post and being knocked down.</li></ul>\n<p><b></b>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ring_corner">Ring corner</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ring corner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg/220px-2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg/330px-2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg/440px-2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017-12-02_Tina_Rupprecht_-_Anne_Sophie_Da_Costa_-_DSC2771.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Female boxer <a href="/wiki/Tina_Rupprecht" title="Tina Rupprecht">Tina Rupprecht</a> receiving instructions from her trainer while being treated by her cutman in the ring corner between rounds.</div></div></div>\n<p>In boxing, each fighter is given a corner of the ring where he rests in between rounds for 1 minute and where his trainers stand. Typically, three men stand in the corner besides the boxer himself; these are the trainer, the assistant trainer and the <a href="/wiki/Cutman" title="Cutman">cutman</a>. The trainer and assistant typically give advice to the boxer on what he is doing wrong as well as encouraging him if he is losing. The cutman is a cutaneous <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">doctor</a> responsible for keeping the boxer\'s face and eyes free of cuts and blood. This is of particular importance because many fights are stopped because of cuts that threaten the boxer\'s eyes.\n</p><p>In addition, the corner is responsible for stopping the fight if they feel their fighter is in grave danger of permanent injury. The corner will occasionally throw in a white towel to signify a boxer\'s surrender (the idiomatic phrase "to throw in the towel", meaning to give up, derives from this practice).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> This can be seen in the fight between <a href="/wiki/Diego_Corrales" title="Diego Corrales">Diego Corrales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Floyd_Mayweather" class="mw-redirect" title="Floyd Mayweather">Floyd Mayweather</a>. In that fight, Corrales\' corner surrendered despite Corrales\' steadfast refusal.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_concerns">Medical concerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Medical concerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Dementia_pugilistica" class="mw-redirect" title="Dementia pugilistica">Dementia pugilistica</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_distance_(boxing)#Distance_change_criticisms" title="The distance (boxing)">The distance (boxing) \xc2\xa7&#160;Distance change criticisms</a></div>\n<p>Knocking a person unconscious or even causing a <a href="/wiki/Concussion" title="Concussion">concussion</a> may cause permanent <a href="/wiki/Brain_damage" title="Brain damage">brain damage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> There is no clear division between the force required to knock a person out and the force likely to kill a person.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> From 1980 to 2007, more than 200 amateur boxers, professional boxers and <a href="/wiki/Toughman_Contest" title="Toughman Contest">Toughman</a> fighters died due to ring or training injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 1983, editorials in the <i>Journal of the <a href="/wiki/American_Medical_Association" title="American Medical Association">American Medical Association</a></i> called for a ban on boxing.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The editor, Dr. George Lundberg, called boxing an "obscenity" that "should not be sanctioned by any civilized society."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Since then, the British,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Canadian<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and Australian<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Medical Associations have called for bans on boxing.\n</p><p>Supporters of the ban state that boxing is the only sport where hurting the other athlete is the goal. Dr. Bill O\'Neill, boxing spokesman for the <a href="/wiki/British_Medical_Association" title="British Medical Association">British Medical Association</a>, has supported the BMA\'s proposed ban on boxing: "It is the only sport where the intention is to inflict serious injury on your opponent, and we feel that we must have a total ban on boxing."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Opponents respond that such a position is misguided opinion, stating that amateur boxing is scored solely according to total connecting blows with no award for "injury". They observe that many skilled professional boxers have had rewarding careers without inflicting injury on opponents by accumulating scoring blows and avoiding punches winning rounds scored 10-9 by the <a href="/wiki/10-point_must_system" class="mw-redirect" title="10-point must system">10-point must system</a>, and they note that there are many other sports where concussions are much more prevalent.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007, one study of amateur boxers showed that protective headgear did not prevent brain damage,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and another found that amateur boxers faced a high risk of brain damage.<sup id="cite_ref-amatneuro_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amatneuro-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The Gothenburg study analyzed temporary levels of neurofiliment light in cerebral spinal fluid which they conclude is evidence of damage, even though the levels soon subside. More comprehensive studies of neurologiocal function on larger samples performed by Johns Hopkins University and accident rates analyzed by <a href="/wiki/National_Safety_Council" title="National Safety Council">National Safety Council</a> show amateur boxing is a comparatively safe sport.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 1997, the American Association of Professional Ringside Physicians was established to create medical protocols through research and education to prevent injuries in boxing.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Professional boxing is forbidden in <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>. It was banned in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> until 2007 when the ban was lifted but strict restrictions, including four three-minute rounds for fights, were imposed.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It was banned in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> from 1965 till the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_communism_in_Albania" title="Fall of communism in Albania">fall of Communism in 1991</a>; it is now legal there. Norway legalized professional boxing in December 2014.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing_Hall_of_Fame">Boxing Hall of Fame</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Boxing Hall of Fame">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gene_Tunney.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Gene_Tunney.jpg/220px-Gene_Tunney.jpg" width="220" height="316" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/Gene_Tunney.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="230" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gene_Tunney.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stamp honoring heavyweight champion <a href="/wiki/Gene_Tunney" title="Gene Tunney">Gene Tunney</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The sport of boxing has two internationally recognized boxing halls of fame; the <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Boxing Hall of Fame">International Boxing Hall of Fame (IBHOF)</a><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and the World Boxing Hall of Fame (WBHF), with the IBHOF being the more widely recognized boxing hall of fame.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, The Boxing Hall of Fame Las Vegas opened in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_NV" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas, NV">Las Vegas, NV</a> founded by <a href="/wiki/Steve_Lott" title="Steve Lott">Steve Lott</a>, former assistant manager for <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The WBHF was founded by Everett L. Sanders in 1980. Since its inception, the WBHOF has never had a permanent location or museum, which has allowed the more recent IBHOF to garner more publicity and prestige. Among the notable names<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> in the WBHF are <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_%22Finito%22_Lopez" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricardo &quot;Finito&quot; Lopez">Ricardo "Finito" Lopez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_%22Flash%22_Elorde" class="mw-redirect" title="Gabriel &quot;Flash&quot; Elorde">Gabriel "Flash" Elorde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Carbajal" title="Michael Carbajal">Michael Carbajal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khaosai_Galaxy" title="Khaosai Galaxy">Khaosai Galaxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Armstrong" title="Henry Armstrong">Henry Armstrong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Johnson_(boxer)" title="Jack Johnson (boxer)">Jack Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Dur%C3%A1n" title="Roberto Dur\xc3\xa1n">Roberto Dur\xc3\xa1n</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Foreman" title="George Foreman">George Foreman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ceferino_Garcia" title="Ceferino Garcia">Ceferino Garcia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Sanchez" class="mw-redirect" title="Salvador Sanchez">Salvador Sanchez</a>. Boxing\'s International Hall of Fame was inspired by a tribute an American town held for two local heroes in 1982. The town, <a href="/wiki/Canastota,_New_York" title="Canastota, New York">Canastota, New York</a>, (which is about 15 miles (24&#160;km) east of Syracuse, via the New York State Thruway), honored former world <a href="/wiki/Welterweight" title="Welterweight">welterweight</a>/<a href="/wiki/Middleweight" title="Middleweight">middleweight</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Basilio" title="Carmen Basilio">Carmen Basilio</a> and his nephew, former world welterweight champion <a href="/wiki/Billy_Backus" title="Billy Backus">Billy Backus</a>. The people of Canastota raised money for the tribute which inspired the idea of creating an official, annual hall of fame for notable boxers.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Hall_of_Fame" title="International Boxing Hall of Fame">International Boxing Hall of Fame</a> opened in Canastota in 1989. The first inductees in 1990 included Jack Johnson, <a href="/wiki/Benny_Leonard" title="Benny Leonard">Benny Leonard</a>, Jack Dempsey, Henry Armstrong, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray_Robinson" title="Sugar Ray Robinson">Sugar Ray Robinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archie_Moore" title="Archie Moore">Archie Moore</a>,  and Muhammad Ali. Other world-class figures<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> include Salvador Sanchez, <a href="/wiki/Jose_Napoles" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Napoles">Jose Napoles</a>, Roberto "Manos de Piedra" Dur\xc3\xa1n, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lopez_(boxer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricardo Lopez (boxer)">Ricardo Lopez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_%22Flash%22_Elorde" class="mw-redirect" title="Gabriel &quot;Flash&quot; Elorde">Gabriel "Flash" Elorde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Saldivar" title="Vicente Saldivar">Vicente Saldivar</a>, Ismael Laguna, Eusebio Pedroza, Carlos Monz\xc3\xb3n, Azumah Nelson, <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Marciano" title="Rocky Marciano">Rocky Marciano</a>, Pipino Cuevas and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Buchanan" title="Ken Buchanan">Ken Buchanan</a>. The Hall of Fame\'s induction ceremony is held every June as part of a four-day event. The fans who come to Canastota for the Induction Weekend are treated to a number of events, including scheduled autograph sessions, boxing exhibitions, a parade featuring past and present inductees, and the induction ceremony itself.\n</p><p>The Boxing Hall of Fame Las Vegas features the $75 million ESPN Classic Sports fight film and tape library and radio broadcast collection. The collection includes the fights of all the great champions including: <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Tyson" title="Mike Tyson">Mike Tyson</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Foreman" title="George Foreman">George Foreman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Duran" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Duran">Roberto Duran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Hagler" class="mw-redirect" title="Marvin Hagler">Marvin Hagler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dempsey" title="Jack Dempsey">Jack Dempsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Louis" title="Joe Louis">Joe Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Frazier" title="Joe Frazier">Joe Frazier</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Marciano" title="Rocky Marciano">Rocky Marciano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray_Robinson" title="Sugar Ray Robinson">Sugar Ray Robinson</a>.  It is this exclusive fight film library that will separate the Boxing Hall of Fame Las Vegas from the other halls of fame which do not have rights to any video of their sports. The inaugural inductees included <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Armstrong" title="Henry Armstrong">Henry Armstrong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Canzoneri" title="Tony Canzoneri">Tony Canzoneri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ezzard_Charles" title="Ezzard Charles">Ezzard Charles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julio_C%C3%A9sar_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Julio C\xc3\xa9sar Ch\xc3\xa1vez">Julio C\xc3\xa9sar Ch\xc3\xa1vez Sr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Dempsey" title="Jack Dempsey">Jack Dempsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Duran" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Duran">Roberto Duran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Louis" title="Joe Louis">Joe Louis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray_Robinson" title="Sugar Ray Robinson">Sugar Ray Robinson</a><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governing_and_sanctioning_bodies">Governing and sanctioning bodies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Governing and sanctioning bodies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_boxing_organisations" title="List of boxing organisations">List of boxing organisations</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wladimir_Klitschko_(2008-12-13).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Wladimir_Klitschko_%282008-12-13%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="293" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wladimir_Klitschko_(2008-12-13).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Federation" title="International Boxing Federation">IBF</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Organization" title="World Boxing Organization">WBO</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Association" title="World Boxing Association">WBA</a> heavyweight champion, Ukrainian <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_Klitschko" title="Wladimir Klitschko">Wladimir Klitschko</a></div></div></div>\n<dl><dt>Governing Bodies</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><a Union">European Boxing Union</a> (EBU)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nevada_Athletic_Commission" title="Nevada Athletic Commission">Nevada State Athletic Commission</a> (NSAC)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Major Council</a> (WBC)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Organization" title="World Boxing Organization">World Boxing Organization</a> (WBO)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Intermediate</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Organization" title="International Boxing Organization">International Boxing Organization</a> (IBO)</li></ul>\n<dl><dt>Amateur</dt></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Association_(amateur)" title="International Boxing Association (amateur)">International Boxing Association</a> (AIBA; now also professional)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing_rankings">Boxing rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boxing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Boxing rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>There are various organization and websites, that rank boxers in both weight class and pound-for-pound manner.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Transnational_Boxing_Rankings_Board" title="Transnational Boxing Rankings Board">Transnational Boxing Rankings Board</a> (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tbrb.org/all-rankings/">ratings</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> (<a
